<p>The <b>London School of Economics</b> (officially the <b>London School of Economics and Political Science</b>, often referred to as  <b>LSE</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> located in London, England, and a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituent college">member institution</a> of the federal <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>. Founded in 1895 by <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Society" title="Fabian Society">Fabian Society</a> members <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Webb,_1st_Baron_Passfield" title="Sidney Webb, 1st Baron Passfield">Sidney Webb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beatrice_Webb" title="Beatrice Webb">Beatrice Webb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graham_Wallas" title="Graham Wallas">Graham Wallas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Bernard_Shaw" title="George Bernard Shaw">George Bernard Shaw</a> for the betterment of society, LSE joined the University of London in 1900 and established its first degree courses under the auspices of the University in 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> LSE started awarding its own degrees in its own name in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-AcademicDress_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AcademicDress-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> prior to which it awarded degrees of the University of London.
</p><p>LSE is located in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">Westminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a>, near the boundary between <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden" title="Covent Garden">Covent Garden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holborn" title="Holborn">Holborn</a>. The area is historically known as <a href="/wiki/Clare_Market" title="Clare Market">Clare Market</a>. The LSE has more than 11,000 students and 3,300 staff, just under seventy percent of whom come from outside the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It had an income of £354.3&#160;million in 2017/18, of which £31.6&#160;million was from research grants.<sup id="cite_ref-LSE_Financial_Statement_17/18_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSE_Financial_Statement_17/18-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> One hundred and fifty-five nationalities are represented amongst LSE's student body and the school has the second highest percentage of international students (70%) of all world universities.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Despite its name, the school is organised into 25 academic departments and institutes which conduct teaching and research across a range of legal studies and social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>LSE is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Commonwealth_Universities" title="Association of Commonwealth Universities">Association of Commonwealth Universities</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_University_Association" title="European University Association">European University Association</a> and is sometimes considered a part of the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_triangle_(universities)" title="Golden triangle (universities)">Golden Triangle</a>" of universities in south-east England. For the subject area of <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social science</a>, LSE places second in the world in the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings"><i>QS Rankings</i></a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> tenth in <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings"><i>THE Rankings</i></a>, and eighth in the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-social_sciences_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-social_sciences-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> LSE is ranked among the top twenty universities nationally by all three UK tables,<sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_University_Guide_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_University_Guide-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> while internationally LSE is ranked in the top 50 by two of the three major global rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Research_Excellence_Framework" title="Research Excellence Framework">Research Excellence Framework</a>, the School had the highest proportion of world-leading research among research submitted of any British non-specialist university.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>LSE has produced many <a href="/wiki/List_of_London_School_of_Economics_people" class="mw-redirect" title="List of London School of Economics people">notable alumni</a> in the fields of law, history, anthropology, economics, philosophy, psychology, business, literature, media and politics. Alumni and staff include 55 past or present heads of state or government and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_the_London_School_of_Economics" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the London School of Economics">18 Nobel laureates</a>. As of 2017, 26% (or 13 out of 49) of all the Nobel Memorial Prizes in Economics have been awarded or jointly awarded to LSE alumni, current staff or former staff, making up 16% (13 out of 79) of all laureates. LSE alumni and staff have also won 3 Nobel Peace Prizes and 2 Nobel Prizes in Literature.<sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_Prize_Winners_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Prize_Winners-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Out of all European universities, LSE has educated the most billionaires according to a 2014 global census of <a href="/wiki/Billionaire" title="Billionaire">U.S dollar billionaires</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_London_School_of_Economics" title="History of the London School of Economics">History of the London School of Economics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb,_c1895_(9259293969).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb%2C_c1895_%289259293969%29.jpg/220px-Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb%2C_c1895_%289259293969%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb%2C_c1895_%289259293969%29.jpg/330px-Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb%2C_c1895_%289259293969%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb%2C_c1895_%289259293969%29.jpg/440px-Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb%2C_c1895_%289259293969%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1732" data-file-height="1235" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beatrice_and_Sidney_Webb,_c1895_(9259293969).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Beatrice_Webb" title="Beatrice Webb">Beatrice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Webb" class="mw-redirect" title="Sidney Webb">Sidney Webb</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The London School of Economics was founded in 1895<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistoryAbout_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistoryAbout-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Beatrice_Webb" title="Beatrice Webb">Beatrice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Webb,_1st_Baron_Passfield" title="Sidney Webb, 1st Baron Passfield">Sidney Webb</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistoryWebbs_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistoryWebbs-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> initially funded by a bequest of £20,000<sup id="cite_ref-SpartacusLSE_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpartacusLSE-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Statisticians_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statisticians-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/Estate_(law)" title="Estate (law)">estate</a> of Henry Hunt Hutchinson. Hutchinson, a lawyer<sup id="cite_ref-SpartacusLSE_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpartacusLSE-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Society" title="Fabian Society">Fabian Society</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SmithLSEandEducation_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SmithLSEandEducation-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LSEPassfieldArchives_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEPassfieldArchives-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> left the money in trust, to be put "towards advancing its [The Fabian Society's] objects in any way they [the <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustees</a>] deem advisable".<sup id="cite_ref-LSEPassfieldArchives_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEPassfieldArchives-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The five trustees were Sidney Webb, <a href="/wiki/Edward_R._Pease" title="Edward R. Pease">Edward Pease</a>, Constance Hutchinson, <a href="/wiki/W._S._de_Mattos" class="mw-redirect" title="W. S. de Mattos">W. S. de Mattos</a> and William Clark.<sup id="cite_ref-SpartacusLSE_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpartacusLSE-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>LSE records that the proposal to establish the school was conceived during a breakfast meeting on 4 August 1894, between the Webbs, Louis Flood and <a href="/wiki/George_Bernard_Shaw" title="George Bernard Shaw">George Bernard Shaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistoryAbout_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistoryAbout-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The proposal was accepted by the trustees in February 1895<sup id="cite_ref-LSEPassfieldArchives_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEPassfieldArchives-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and LSE held its first classes in October of that year, in rooms at 9 John Street, <a href="/wiki/Adelphi,_London" title="Adelphi, London">Adelphi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistory1895_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistory1895-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The School joined the federal <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a> in 1900, and was recognised as a Faculty of Economics of the university. The University of London degrees of BSc (Econ) and DSc (Econ) were established in 1901, the first university degrees dedicated to the social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistory1895_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistory1895-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Expanding rapidly over the following years, the school moved initially to the nearby 10 Adelphi Terrace, then to Clare Market and Houghton Street. The foundation stone of the Old Building, on Houghton Street, was laid by <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">King George V</a> in 1920;<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistoryAbout_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistoryAbout-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> the building was opened in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistory1895_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistory1895-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedrich_Hayek_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Friedrich_Hayek_portrait.jpg/220px-Friedrich_Hayek_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7f/Friedrich_Hayek_portrait.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedrich_Hayek_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Friedrich Hayek</a>, who taught at LSE during the 1930s and 1940s</div></div></div>
<p>The 1930s economic debate between LSE and Cambridge is well known in academic circles. Rivalry between academic opinion at LSE and Cambridge goes back to the school's roots when LSE's <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Cannan" title="Edwin Cannan">Edwin Cannan</a> (1861–1935), Professor of Economics, and Cambridge's Professor of Political Economy, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Marshall" title="Alfred Marshall">Alfred Marshall</a> (1842–1924), the leading economist of the day, argued about the bedrock matter of economics and whether the subject should be considered as an organic whole. (Marshall disapproved of LSE's separate listing of pure theory and its insistence on economic history).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The dispute also concerned the question of the economist's role, and whether this should be as a detached expert or a practical adviser.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Despite the traditional view that the LSE and Cambridge were fierce rivals through the 1920s and 30s, they worked together in the 1920s on the London and Cambridge Economic Service.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> However, the 1930s brought a return to disputes as economists at the two universities argued over how best to address the economic problems caused by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CambDebate_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CambDebate-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main figures in this debate were <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">John Maynard Keynes</a> from Cambridge and the LSE's <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Friedrich Hayek</a>. The LSE Economist <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Robbins" title="Lionel Robbins">Lionel Robbins</a> was also heavily involved. Starting off as a disagreement over whether demand management or deflation was the better solution to the economic problems of the time, it eventually embraced much wider concepts of economics and macroeconomics. Keynes put forward the theories now known as <a href="/wiki/Keynesian_economics" title="Keynesian economics">Keynesian economics</a>, involving the active participation of the state and public sector, while Hayek and Robbins followed the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_School" title="Austrian School">Austrian School</a>, which emphasised free trade and opposed state involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-CambDebate_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CambDebate-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During World War II, the School decamped from London to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>, occupying buildings belonging to <a href="/wiki/Peterhouse,_Cambridge" title="Peterhouse, Cambridge">Peterhouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The School's arms,<sup id="cite_ref-PlantArms_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlantArms-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> including its motto and beaver mascot, were adopted in February 1922,<sup id="cite_ref-IOEBeginnings_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IOEBeginnings-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> on the recommendation of a committee of twelve, including eight students, which was established to research the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-LSEBeaverClub_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEBeaverClub-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Latin motto, <i>"Rerum cognoscere causas"</i>, is taken from <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Georgics" title="Georgics">Georgics</a>. Its English translation is "to Know the Causes of Things"<sup id="cite_ref-IOEBeginnings_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IOEBeginnings-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and it was suggested by Professor <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Cannan" title="Edwin Cannan">Edwin Cannan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LSEHistoryAbout_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEHistoryAbout-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The beaver mascot was selected for its associations with "foresight, constructiveness and industrious behaviour".<sup id="cite_ref-LSEBeaverClub_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSEBeaverClub-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lse_initials.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Lse_initials.jpg/150px-Lse_initials.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Lse_initials.jpg/225px-Lse_initials.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Lse_initials.jpg/300px-Lse_initials.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lse_initials.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stonework featuring the initials of LSE</div></div></div>
<p>LSE continues to have a wide impact within British society, through its relationships and influence in politics, business and law.  <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> described such influence in 2005 when it stated:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Once again the political clout of the school, which seems to be closely wired into parliament, Whitehall and the Bank of England, is being felt by ministers.... The strength of LSE is that it is close to the political process: <a href="/wiki/Mervyn_King,_Baron_King_of_Lothbury" title="Mervyn King, Baron King of Lothbury">Mervyn King</a>, was a former LSE professor. The chairman of the House of Commons education committee, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Sheerman" title="Barry Sheerman">Barry Sheerman</a>, sits on its board of governors, along with Labour peer <a href="/wiki/Frank_Judd,_Baron_Judd" title="Frank Judd, Baron Judd">Lord (Frank) Judd</a>. Also on the board are Tory MPs <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Bottomley" title="Virginia Bottomley">Virginia Bottomley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Shepherd" title="Richard Shepherd">Richard Shepherd</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Saatchi,_Baron_Saatchi" title="Maurice Saatchi, Baron Saatchi">Lord Saatchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elspeth_Howe,_Baroness_Howe_of_Idlicote" title="Elspeth Howe, Baroness Howe of Idlicote">Lady Howe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Commenting in 2001 on the rising status of the LSE, the British magazine <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> stated that "two decades ago the LSE was still the poor relation of the University of London's other colleges. Now... it regularly follows Oxford and Cambridge in league tables of research output and teaching quality and is at least as well-known abroad as Oxbridge". According to the magazine, the School "owes its success to the single-minded, American-style exploitation of its brand name and political connections by the recent directors, particularly Mr <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Giddens" title="Anthony Giddens">Giddens</a> and his predecessor, <a href="/wiki/John_Ashworth_(biologist)" title="John Ashworth (biologist)">John Ashworth</a>" and raises money from foreign students' high fees, which are attracted by academic stars such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Sennett" title="Richard Sennett">Richard Sennett</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2006, the School was active in opposing British government proposals to introduce compulsory ID cards,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> researching into the associated costs of the scheme, and shifting public and government opinion on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The institution is also popular with politicians and <a href="/wiki/Members_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of Parliament">MPs</a> to launch new policy, legislation and manifesto pledges, prominently with the launch of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> Manifesto Conference under <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">Nick Clegg</a> on 12 January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_to_present">2010 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg/150px-Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg/225px-Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg/300px-Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2314" data-file-height="3300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nemat_Shafik_Portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nemat_Shafik" title="Nemat Shafik">Nemat Shafik</a> is the director of LSE<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the early 2010s, its academics have been at the forefront of both national and international government consultations, reviews and policy, including representation on the UK Airports Commission,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Independent Police Commission,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Migration Advisory Committee,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> UN Advisory Board on Water and Sanitation,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> London Finance Commission,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">HS2 Limited</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> the UK government's Infrastructure Commission<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and advising on Architecture and Urbanism for the London 2012 Olympics<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Craig_Calhoun" title="Craig Calhoun">Craig Calhoun</a> took up the post of Director in September 2012. Its previous Director, <a href="/wiki/Judith_Rees" title="Judith Rees">Judith Rees</a>, is also chair of the school's Grantham Institute on Climate Change, an adviser to the World Bank as well as sitting on the UN Secretary General's Advisory Board on Water and Sanitation and the International Scientific Advisory Council (ISAC).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> She is also a former Convenor of the Department of Geography and Environment and served as Deputy Director from 1998–2004.
</p><p>In February 2016, Calhoun announced his intention to step down at the end of the academic year, in order to become president of the <a href="/wiki/Berggruen_Institute" title="Berggruen Institute">Berggruen Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In September 2016, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> Deputy Governor <a href="/wiki/Minouche_Shafik" class="mw-redirect" title="Minouche Shafik">Dame Nemat Shafik</a> was announced to replace Professor <a href="/wiki/Julia_Black" title="Julia Black">Julia Black</a> as the School's director. Shafik began to lead the LSE in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics_Gaddafi_links" class="mw-redirect" title="London School of Economics Gaddafi links">London School of Economics Gaddafi links</a></div>
<p>In February 2011, LSE had to face the consequences of <a href="/wiki/Matriculate" class="mw-redirect" title="Matriculate">matriculating</a> one of <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>'s sons, while accepting a £1.5m donation to the university from his family.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> LSE director Howard Davies resigned over allegations about the institution's links to the Libyan regime.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The LSE announced in a statement that it had accepted his resignation with "great regret" and that it had set up an external inquiry into the school's relationship with the Libyan regime and Saif al-Islam Gaddafi, to be conducted by the former lord chief justice <a href="/wiki/Harry_Woolf,_Baron_Woolf" title="Harry Woolf, Baron Woolf">Harry Woolf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, the LSE was featured in a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Panorama_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Panorama (TV series)">Panorama</a></i> documentary on North Korea, filmed inside the repressive regime by undercover journalists attached to a trip by the LSE's Grimshaw Society, a <a href="/wiki/Student_society" title="Student society">student society</a> of the international relations department. The trip had been sanctioned by high-level North Korean officials.<sup id="cite_ref-NewsAUPanorama_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewsAUPanorama-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Conlan_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conlan-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The trip caused international media attention, as a BBC journalist was posing as a part of LSE.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> There was debate as to where this put the student's lives in jeopardy in the repressive regime if a reporter had been exposed.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The North Korea government made hostile threats towards the students and LSE, after the publicity, which forced an apology from the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-Conlan_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conlan-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2015, it was revealed that the university was paid approximately £40,000 for a "glowing report" for <a href="/wiki/Camila_Batmanghelidjh" title="Camila Batmanghelidjh">Camila Batmanghelidjh</a>'s charity, <a href="/wiki/Kids_Company" title="Kids Company">Kids Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The study was used by Batmanghelidjh to prove that the charity provided good value for money and was well managed. The university did not disclose that the study was funded by the charity and claims made by the report have since been discredited.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Tabloid newspapers are not ideal sources. (January 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the summer of 2017, dozens of LSE cleaners contracted via Noonan Services went on weekly strikes across the campus, causing significant disruption during end of year examinations.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The dispute organised by the <a href="/wiki/United_Voices_of_the_World" title="United Voices of the World">UVW union</a> was originally over unwarranted dismissals of cleaners, but had escalated into a broad demand for decent employment rights matching those of LSE's in-house employees.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Owen_Jones_(writer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Owen Jones (writer)">Owen Jones</a> did not cross the picket line after arriving for a debate on grammar schools with Peter Hitchens.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> It was announced in June 2017 that all outsourced workers at the LSE would be offered in-house contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_World_Turned_Upside_Down"><i>The World Turned Upside Down</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The World Turned Upside Down">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_(sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_%28sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger%29.jpg/170px-The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_%28sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_%28sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger%29.jpg/255px-The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_%28sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_%28sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger%29.jpg/340px-The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_%28sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2732" data-file-height="3643" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_(sculpture_by_Mark_Wallinger).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The World Turned Upside Down</i>. The island of Taiwan is coloured differently from mainland China</div></div></div>
<p>A sculpture by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wallinger" title="Mark Wallinger">Mark Wallinger</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Turned_Upside_Down_(sculpture)" title="The World Turned Upside Down (sculpture)">The World Turned Upside Down</a></i>, which features a globe resting on its north pole, was installed in Sheffield Street on the LSE campus on 26 March 2019. The artwork attracted controversy for showing the island of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> as a sovereign entity, rather than as part of the <a href="/wiki/People%E2%80%99s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People’s Republic of China">People’s Republic of China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a> being denoted as a full capital and featuring internationally recognised <a href="/wiki/Sino-Indian_border_dispute" title="Sino-Indian border dispute">boundaries between India and China</a>. 
</p><p>After protests and reactions from both sides,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> the school made the decision to alter the work of art over the objections of the Taiwanese students.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The university decided later that year that it would retain the original design which chromatically displayed the PRC and Taiwan as different entities but with the addition of an asterisk beside the name of Taiwan and a corresponding placard that clarified the institution's position regarding the controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_and_estate">Campus and estate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Campus and estate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE_main_entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/LSE_main_entrance.jpg/220px-LSE_main_entrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/LSE_main_entrance.jpg/330px-LSE_main_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/LSE_main_entrance.jpg/440px-LSE_main_entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE_main_entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>LSE's Old Building</div></div></div>
<p>Since 1902, LSE has been based at <a href="/wiki/Clare_Market" title="Clare Market">Clare Market</a> and Houghton Street in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">Westminster</a>. It is surrounded by a number of important institutions including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Courts_of_Justice" title="Royal Courts of Justice">Royal Courts of Justice</a>, all four <a href="/wiki/Inns_of_Court" title="Inns of Court">Inns of Courts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Surgeons" title="Royal College of Surgeons">Royal College of Surgeons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Soane%27s_Museum" title="Sir John Soane&#39;s Museum">Sir John Soane's Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a> is immediately across <a href="/wiki/Kingsway,_London" title="Kingsway, London">Kingsway</a> from campus, which also borders the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> and is within walking distance to <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_Square" title="Trafalgar Square">Trafalgar Square</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of Parliament">Houses of Parliament</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Land_Registry_Offices,_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/The_Land_Registry_Offices%2C_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg/220px-The_Land_Registry_Offices%2C_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/The_Land_Registry_Offices%2C_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg/330px-The_Land_Registry_Offices%2C_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/The_Land_Registry_Offices%2C_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg/440px-The_Land_Registry_Offices%2C_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Land_Registry_Offices,_Lincoln_Inn_Fields.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/32_Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields" title="32 Lincoln&#39;s Inn Fields">32 Lincoln's Inn Fields</a> houses the Department of Economics and the <a href="/wiki/International_Growth_Centre" title="International Growth Centre">International Growth Centre</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1920, <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">King George V</a> laid the foundation of the Old Building. The campus now occupies an almost continuous group of around 30 buildings between <a href="/wiki/Kingsway,_London" title="Kingsway, London">Kingsway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aldwych" title="Aldwych">Aldwych</a>. Alongside teaching and academic space, the institution also owns 11 student halls of residence across London, two public houses, a West End theatre (the <a href="/wiki/Peacock_Theatre" title="Peacock Theatre">Peacock</a>), early years centre, <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">NHS</a> medical centre and extensive sports ground in Berrylands, south London.  The School's campus is noted for its numerous public art installations which include <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wilson_(sculptor)" title="Richard Wilson (sculptor)">Richard Wilson</a>'s <i>Square the Block</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Michael Brown's <i>Blue Rain</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Le_Brun" title="Christopher Le Brun">Christopher Le Brun</a>'s <i>Desert Window</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the early 2000s, the entire campus has undergone an extensive refurbishment project and a major fund-raising "Campaign for LSE" raised over £100 million in what was one of the largest university fund-raising exercises outside North America.  This process was begun with the £35 million renovation of the Lionel Robbins Building by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Foster">Sir Norman Foster</a> to house the <a href="/wiki/British_Library_of_Political_and_Economic_Science" title="British Library of Political and Economic Science">British Library of Political and Economic Science</a> (BLPES), the world's largest social science and political library and the second largest single entity library in Britain, after the British Library at King's Cross.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NABuilding.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NABuilding.JPG/220px-NABuilding.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NABuilding.JPG/330px-NABuilding.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NABuilding.JPG/440px-NABuilding.JPG 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="418" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NABuilding.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The New Academic Building houses the Departments of Management and Law</div></div></div>
<p>In 2003, LSE purchased the former Public Trustee building at 24 Kingsway, and engaged <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Grimshaw" title="Nicholas Grimshaw">Sir Nicholas Grimshaw</a> to redesign it into an ultra-modern educational facility at a total cost of over £45&#160;million – increasing the size of the campus by 120,000 square feet (11,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>). The New Academic Building opened for teaching in October 2008, with an official opening by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Her Majesty the Queen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Duke of Edinburgh</a> on 5 November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Academic_Building_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Academic_Building-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In November 2009 the School purchased the adjacent Sardinia House to house three academic departments and the nearby Old White Horse public house, before acquiring the freehold of the grade-II listed <a href="/wiki/HM_Land_Registry" title="HM Land Registry">Land Registry Building</a> at <a href="/wiki/32_Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields" title="32 Lincoln&#39;s Inn Fields">32 Lincoln's Inn Fields</a> in October 2010, which was reopened in March 2013 by <a href="/wiki/The_Princess_Royal" class="mw-redirect" title="The Princess Royal">The Princess Royal</a> as the new home for the Department of Economics, <a href="/wiki/International_Growth_Centre" title="International Growth Centre">International Growth Centre</a> and its associated economic research centres.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saw_Swee_Hock_Student_Centre">Saw Swee Hock Student Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Saw Swee Hock Student Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
The first new building on the site for more than 40 years, the Saw Swee Hock Student Centre, opened in January 2014 following an <a href="/wiki/Architectural_design_competition" title="Architectural design competition">architectural design competition</a> managed by <a href="/wiki/RIBA_Competitions" title="RIBA Competitions">RIBA Competitions</a>. The building provides new accommodation for the <a href="/wiki/LSE_Students%27_Union" title="LSE Students&#39; Union">LSE Students' Union</a>, LSE accommodation office and LSE careers service as well as a bar, events space, gymnasium, rooftop terrace, learning café, dance studio and media centre.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The building, designed as a showpiece for the City of Westminster and Midtown was recognised as having a low environmental impact receiving an 'Outstanding' status under BREEAM, and in 2012 was one of three winners of the New London Award in the Education category.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In May 2014 the Saw Swee Hock Student Centre won the RIBA London Building of the Year Award.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OldCuriosityShop.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/OldCuriosityShop.JPG/220px-OldCuriosityShop.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/OldCuriosityShop.JPG/330px-OldCuriosityShop.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/OldCuriosityShop.JPG/440px-OldCuriosityShop.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OldCuriosityShop.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 16th century <a href="/wiki/Old_Curiosity_Shop" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Curiosity Shop">Old Curiosity Shop</a>. While independent from the university, the house is surrounded by properties of the LSE</div></div></div><p><b><big>Centre Building</big></b>
</p><p>The new Centre Building, situated opposite the <a href="/wiki/British_Library_of_Political_and_Economic_Science" title="British Library of Political and Economic Science">British Library of Political and Economic Science</a>, opened in June 2019. Designed as both a teaching and an academic space, the new 13-storey Centre Building includes 14 seminar rooms seating between 20 and 60, 234 study spaces, a 200-seater auditorium, as well as three lecture theatres.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The building hosts the Department of Government on Levels 3 and 4, the International Inequalities Institute on Levels 4 and 5, and the Department of International Relations on Levels 7 through 10, and the Directorate on Level 1. The roof terraces on levels 2, 6 and 12 are also accessible to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg/220px-View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg/330px-View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg/440px-View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="967" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_LSE_from_NAB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>LSE Campus as viewed from the terrace of the New Academic Building in January 2018, showing the Centre Buildings redevelopment and the demolition of 44 Lincoln's Inn Fields</div></div></div>
<p>It is currently embarking on redevelopment and expansion with the development of a £120 million new facility designed by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rogers" title="Richard Rogers">Rogers Stirk Harbour &amp; Partners</a> following the completion of a global design competition managed by <a href="/wiki/RIBA_Competitions" title="RIBA Competitions">RIBA Competitions</a>.  Once complete in 2018 the new development - the Global Centre for the Social Sciences
- will house the Departments of Government, International Relations and the European Institute and feature a new square at the centre of the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In September 2013, LSE purchased the freehold of 44 <a href="/wiki/Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields" title="Lincoln&#39;s Inn Fields">Lincoln's Inn Fields</a>, previously the home of the Francis Crick Institute's laboratories until 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The building will be demolished in 2017 to make way for the new <a href="/wiki/Paul_Marshall_(investor)" title="Paul Marshall (investor)">Paul Marshall</a> Building which will house academic departments (Management, Accounting and Finance), sports facilities and the new Marshall Institute for Philanthropy and Social Entrepreneurship.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, LSE brought its ownership of buildings on Lincoln's Inn Fields to six with the purchase of 5 Lincoln's Inn Fields on the north side of the square which has since been converted into faculty accommodation.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 November 2017, LSE announced that it has achieved contract completion on the purchase to acquire the Nuffield Building, which is adjacent to the Lincoln's Inn Fields, from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Surgeons_of_England" title="Royal College of Surgeons of England">Royal College of Surgeons</a>. According to the contract the building will be transferred to LSE after renovations in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lse_george_iv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/53/Lse_george_iv.jpg/170px-Lse_george_iv.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/53/Lse_george_iv.jpg/255px-Lse_george_iv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/53/Lse_george_iv.jpg/340px-Lse_george_iv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lse_george_iv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The George IV, a pub owned by LSE</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The nearest <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> stations are <a href="/wiki/Holborn_tube_station" title="Holborn tube station">Holborn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temple_tube_station" title="Temple tube station">Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden_tube_station" title="Covent Garden tube station">Covent Garden</a>. <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross_tube_station" title="Charing Cross tube station">Charing Cross</a>, at the Trafalgar Square end of Strand, and the <a href="/wiki/City_Thameslink_railway_station" title="City Thameslink railway station">City Thameslink</a> entrance at <a href="/wiki/Ludgate_Hill" title="Ludgate Hill">Ludgate Hill</a> are the nearest mainline stations, whilst <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">London Waterloo</a> is a walk or bus across the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>. Buses to <a href="/wiki/Aldwych" title="Aldwych">Aldwych</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingsway,_London" title="Kingsway, London">Kingsway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Courts_of_Justice" title="Royal Courts of Justice">Royal Courts of Justice</a> contain stops which are designated as 'alight here for LSE'.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_and_administration">Organisation and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Organisation and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although LSE is a constituent college of the federal University of London, it is in many ways comparable with free-standing, self-governing and independently funded universities, and it awards its own degrees.
</p><p>LSE is incorporated under the <a href="/wiki/Companies_Act" title="Companies Act">Companies Act</a> as a company limited by guarantee and is an exempt charity within the meaning of Schedule Two of the <a href="/wiki/Charities_Act_1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Charities Act 1993">Charities Act 1993</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The principal governance bodies of the LSE are: the LSE Council; the Court of Governors; the Academic Board; and the Director and Director's Management Team.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The LSE Council is responsible for strategy and its members are company directors of the school. It has specific responsibilities in relation to areas including: the monitoring of institutional performance; finance and financial sustainability; audit arrangements; estate strategy; human resource and employment policy; health and safety; "educational character and mission", and student experience. The council is supported in carrying out its role by a number of committees which report directly to it.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Court of Governors deals with certain constitutional matters and has pre-decision discussions on key policy issues and the involvement of individual governors in the school's activities. The court has the following formal powers: the appointment of members of court, its subcommittees and of the council; election of the chair and vice chairs of the court and council and honorary fellows of the School; the amendment of the Memorandum and Articles of Association; and the appointment of external auditors.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_95-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Academic Board is LSE's principal academic body, and considers all major issues of general policy affecting the academic life of the School and its development. It is chaired by the director, with staff and student membership, and is supported by its own structure of committees. The Vice Chair of the Academic Board serves as a non-director member of the council and makes a termly report to the Council.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_95-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Director">Director</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Director">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Ashworth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/John_Ashworth.jpg/150px-John_Ashworth.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/John_Ashworth.jpg/225px-John_Ashworth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/John_Ashworth.jpg/300px-John_Ashworth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="897" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Ashworth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Ashworth_(vice-chancellor)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Ashworth (vice-chancellor)">Sir John Ashworth</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg/150px-Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg/225px-Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg/300px-Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1866" data-file-height="2675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Professor_Craig_Calhoun.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Craig_Calhoun" title="Craig Calhoun">Craig Calhoun</a></div></div></div>
<p>The director is the head of LSE and its chief executive officer, responsible for executive management and leadership on academic issues. The director reports to and is accountable to the Council. The director is also the accountable officer for the purposes of the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Funding_Council_for_England" title="Higher Education Funding Council for England">Higher Education Funding Council for England</a> Financial Memorandum. The LSE's current director is <a href="/wiki/Minouche_Shafik" class="mw-redirect" title="Minouche Shafik">Dame Nemat Shafik</a>, who replaced interim director, Professor <a href="/wiki/Julia_Black" title="Julia Black">Julia Black</a>, on 1 September 2017.
</p><p>The director is supported by a deputy director and provost who oversees the heads of academic departments and institutes, three pro-directors each with designated portfolios (teaching and learning, research and planning and resources) and the School secretary who acts as company secretary.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_departments_and_institutes">Academic departments and institutes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Academic departments and institutes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LSE's research and teaching is organised into a network of independent academic departments established by the LSE Council, the School's governing body, on the advice of the Academic Board, the School's senior academic authority.  There are currently 27 academic departments or institutes.
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; -webkit-column-width: 25em; column-width: 25em;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The LSE group has an endowment (as of 31 July 2016) of £119M and had a total income for 2015–16 (excluding donations and endowments) of £311M (£293M in 2014–15) with expenditure of £307M (2014–15 £302M). Key sources of income included £177M from tuition fees and education contacts (2014–15 £167M), £25M from funding council grants (2014–15 £22M), £32M from research grants (2014–15 – £27M) and £5.3M from investment income (2014–15 £4.7M).<sup id="cite_ref-financial_statement_2016_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financial_statement_2016-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> Pay Survey 2017 revealed that, among larger, non-specialist institutions, LSE professors and academics were the highest paid in the UK, with average incomes of £103,886 and £65,177 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Endowment">Endowment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Endowment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The London School of Economics (LSE) is aiming to increase the size of its endowment fund to more than £1bn, which would make it one of the best resourced institutions in the UK and the world. The effort was initiated in 2016 by Lord Myners, then chairman of the LSE's Council and Court of Governors. The plan includes working with wealthy alumni of LSE to make large contributions, increasing the annual budget surplus, and launching a new, widescale alumni donor campaign. The plan to grow LSE's endowment to more than £1bn has been continued by Lord Myners' successors at the LSE.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The LSE has stated that currently "limited endowment funding constrains our ability to offer 'needs blind' admission to students".<sup id="cite_ref-financial_statement_2016_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financial_statement_2016-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_year">Academic year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Academic year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LSE continues to adopt a three-term structure and has not moved to semesters. <a href="/wiki/Michaelmas_Term" class="mw-redirect" title="Michaelmas Term">Michaelmas Term</a> runs from October to mid-December, <a href="/wiki/Lent_Term" class="mw-redirect" title="Lent Term">Lent Term</a> from mid-January to late March and Summer Term from late April to mid-June.  Certain departments operate reading weeks in early November and mid-February.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Logo.2C_arms_and_mascot"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo,_arms_and_mascot">Logo, arms and mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Logo, arms and mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/LSE_Logo.svg/150px-LSE_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/LSE_Logo.svg/225px-LSE_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/LSE_Logo.svg/300px-LSE_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>LSE's "red block" logo</div></div></div>
<p>The school's historic coat of arms is used on official documentation including degree certificates and transcripts and includes the motto – <i>rerum cognoscere causas</i>, a line taken from <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>’s <i><a href="/wiki/Georgics" title="Georgics">Georgics</a></i> meaning "to know the causes of things", together with the school's mascot – a beaver. Both these symbols, adopted in February 1922, continue to be held in high regard to this day with the beaver chosen because of its representation as "a hard working and industrious yet sociable animal", attributes that the founders hoped LSE students to both possess and aspire to.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The school's weekly newspaper is still entitled <i>The Beaver</i>, Rosebery residence hall's bar is called the Tipsy Beaver and LSE sports teams are known as the Beavers.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The institution has two sets of colours – brand and academic – red being the brand colour used on signage, publications and in buildings across campus and purple, black and gold for academic purposes including presentation ceremonies and graduation dress.
</p><p>LSE's present 'red block' logo was adopted as part of a rebrand in the early 2000s, before which the school's coat of arms was used exclusively to represent the institution. As a trademarked brand, it is carefully protected but can be produced in various forms to reflect different requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>  In its full form it contains the full name of the institution to the right of the block with a further small empty red square at the end, but it is adapted for each academic department or professional service division to provide a cohesive brand across the institution.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_profile">Academic profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Academic profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
