<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE-mosa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/LSE-mosa.jpg/220px-LSE-mosa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/LSE-mosa.jpg/330px-LSE-mosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/LSE-mosa.jpg/440px-LSE-mosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE-mosa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Clement's Building</div></div></div>
<p>Admission to LSE is highly competitive: the school received 20,000 applications for 1,600 undergraduate places in 2017, or 12.5 applicants per place.<sup id="cite_ref-Applications_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Applications-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> All undergraduate applications, including international applications, are made through <a href="/wiki/UCAS" title="UCAS">UCAS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Applications_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Applications-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> LSE had the 4th highest average entry qualification for undergraduates of any UK university in 2015-16, with new students averaging 537 <a href="/wiki/UCAS_Tariff" title="UCAS Tariff">UCAS points</a> (pre-2017 tariff),<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> equivalent to just below A*A*A*A in <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level_(United_Kingdom)" title="GCE Advanced Level (United Kingdom)">A-level</a> grades.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The university gives offers of admission to 37.0% of its applicants, the 3rd lowest amongst the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> For 2017 entry, the university was one of only a few mainstream universities (along with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">UCL</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warwick" title="University of Warwick">Warwick</a>) to have no courses available in <a href="/wiki/UCAS#Confirmation_and_clearing" title="UCAS">Clearing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Postgraduate students at the LSE are required to have a first or upper second Class UK <a href="/wiki/Honours_degree" title="Honours degree">honours degree</a>, or its foreign equivalent for master's degrees, while direct entry to the MPhil/PhD programme requires a UK taught master's with merit or foreign equivalent. Admission to the diploma requires as UK degree or equivalent plus relevant experience.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The intake to applications ratio for postgraduate degree programmes is very competitive; the MSc Financial Mathematics had a ratio of just over 4% in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>31.6% of LSE's undergraduates are <a href="/wiki/Independent_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Independent school (United Kingdom)">privately educated</a>, the ninth highest proportion amongst mainstream British universities.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In the 2016-17 academic year, the university had a domicile breakdown of 33:18:50 of UK:EU:non-EU students respectively with a female to male ratio of 52:47.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Programmes_and_degrees">Programmes and degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Programmes and degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LSE is the only university in the United Kingdom dedicated solely to the study and research of social sciences. LSE awards a range of academic degrees spanning bachelors, masters and PhDs. The post-nominals awarded are the degree abbreviations used commonly among British universities.
</p><p>
The School offers over 140 <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">MSc</a> programmes, 5 <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Public_Administration" title="Master of Public Administration">MPA</a> programmes, an <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Laws" title="Master of Laws">LLM</a>, 30 <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">BSc</a> programmes, an <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Laws" title="Bachelor of Laws">LLB</a>, 4 <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">BA</a> programmes (including International History and Geography), and 35 PhD programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Other subjects pioneered by LSE include anthropology, criminology, social psychology, sociology and social policy; with international relations being first taught as a discipline at LSE.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Courses are split across more than thirty research centres and nineteen departments, plus a Language Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holborn,_John_Watkins_Plaza,_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Holborn%2C_John_Watkins_Plaza%2C_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg/220px-Holborn%2C_John_Watkins_Plaza%2C_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Holborn%2C_John_Watkins_Plaza%2C_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg/330px-Holborn%2C_John_Watkins_Plaza%2C_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Holborn%2C_John_Watkins_Plaza%2C_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg/440px-Holborn%2C_John_Watkins_Plaza%2C_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holborn,_John_Watkins_Plaza,_London_School_of_Economics_-_geograph.org.uk_-_668683.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John Watkins Plaza at the London School of Economics</div></div></div><p>Since programmes are all within the social sciences, they closely resemble each other, and undergraduate students usually take at least one course module in a subject outside of their degree for their first and second years of study, promoting a broader education in the social sciences.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> At undergraduate level, some departments have as few as 90 students across the three years of study.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Since September 2010,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> it has been compulsory for first year undergraduates to participate in LSE 100: Understanding the Causes of Things alongside normal studies.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1902, following its absorption into the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>, and up until 2007, all degrees were awarded by the federal university, in common with all other colleges of the university. This system was changed in 2007 to enable some colleges to award their own degrees.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> LSE was granted the power to begin awarding its own degrees from July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-AcademicDress_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AcademicDress-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> All students entering from the 2007-8 academic year onwards received an LSE degree, while students who started before this date were issued University of London degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In conjunction with <a href="/wiki/NYU_Stern" class="mw-redirect" title="NYU Stern">NYU Stern</a> and <a href="/wiki/HEC_Paris" title="HEC Paris">HEC Paris</a>, LSE also offers the <a href="/wiki/TRIUM_EMBA" title="TRIUM EMBA">TRIUM Executive MBA</a>. This was globally ranked third among executive MBAs by the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Research_Excellence_Framework" title="Research Excellence Framework">Research Excellence Framework</a>, LSE had the joint highest percentage of world-leading research among research submitted of any institution that entered more than one unit of assessment<sup id="cite_ref-THEREF2014_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THEREF2014-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and was ranked third by cumulative grade point average with a score of 3.35, beating both Oxford and Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> It was ranked 23rd in the country for research power by <a href="/wiki/Research_Fortnight" title="Research Fortnight">Research Fortnight</a> based on its REF2014 results, and 28th in research power by the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-THEREF2014_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THEREF2014-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ResearchPower_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ResearchPower-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> This followed the <a href="/wiki/Research_Assessment_Exercise" title="Research Assessment Exercise">Research Assessment Exercise</a> in 2008 where the School was placed second equal nationally on GPA, first for fraction of world-leading (4*) research and fourth for fraction of world-leading or internationally excellent (3* and 4*) research in LSE's analysis of the results,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> fourth equal for GPA and 29th for research power in Times Higher Education's analysis,<sup id="cite_ref-THEREF2014_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THEREF2014-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and 27th in research power by Research Fortnight's analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-ResearchPower_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ResearchPower-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to analysis of the REF 2014 subject results by Times Higher Education, the School is the UK's top research university in terms of GPA of research submitted in business and management; area studies; and communication, cultural and media studies, library and information management, and second in law; politics and international studies; economics and econometrics; and social work and social policy.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HoughtonStreet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/HoughtonStreet.jpg/220px-HoughtonStreet.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/HoughtonStreet.jpg/330px-HoughtonStreet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/HoughtonStreet.jpg/440px-HoughtonStreet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HoughtonStreet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Houghton Street is the centre of the LSE campus</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_centres">Research centres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Research centres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The School houses a number of notable centres including the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_the_Analysis_of_Social_Exclusion" title="Centre for the Analysis of Social Exclusion">Centre for the Analysis of Social Exclusion</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Climate_Change_Economics_and_Policy" title="Centre for Climate Change Economics and Policy">Centre for Climate Change Economics and Policy</a>, the Centre for Macroeconomics, Centre for Economic Performance, LSE Health and Social Care, the Financial Markets Group (founded by former <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> governor <a href="/wiki/Mervyn_King,_Baron_King_of_Lothbury" title="Mervyn King, Baron King of Lothbury">Sir Mervyn King</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Grantham_Research_Institute_on_Climate_Change_and_the_Environment" title="Grantham Research Institute on Climate Change and the Environment">Grantham Research Institute on Climate Change and the Environment</a> (chaired by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Stern" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas Stern">Lord Stern</a>), <a href="/wiki/LSE_Cities" title="LSE Cities">LSE Cities</a>, the UK <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a> funded <a href="/wiki/International_Growth_Centre" title="International Growth Centre">International Growth Centre</a> and one of the six the UK government-backed 'What Works Centres' – the What Works Centre for Local Economic Growth.  The <a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Group" title="Greater London Group">Greater London Group</a> was influential research centre within LSE from the late 1950s on, before being subsumed into the <a href="/w/index.php?title=LSE_London&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="LSE London (page does not exist)">LSE London</a> research group.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="LSE_Institute_of_Global_Affairs">LSE Institute of Global Affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: LSE Institute of Global Affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In late 2014, LSE hired <a href="/wiki/Erik_Bergl%C3%B6f" title="Erik Berglöf">Erik Berglöf</a>, former Chief Economist and Special Advisor to the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">EBRD</a> to establish a new Institute of Global Affairs with seven regional research centres focusing on Africa, East Asia, Latin America and the Caribbean, the Middle East, South Asia, South East Asia and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>  It is joined by the <a href="/wiki/LSE_IDEAS" title="LSE IDEAS">LSE IDEAS</a> think tank, which in a global survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> in 2015 was jointly ranked as world's second-best university think tanks for the third year running alongside the LSE Public Policy Group, after <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Belfer_Center_for_Science_and_International_Affairs" title="Belfer Center for Science and International Affairs">Belfer Center for Science and International Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2015, <a href="/wiki/Angelina_Jolie" title="Angelina Jolie">Angelina Jolie</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">William Hague</a> launched the UK's first academic Centre on Women, Peace and Security, based at the School. The Centre aims to contribute to global women's rights issues, including the prosecution of war rape and women's engagement in politics, through academic research, a post-graduate teaching program, public engagement, and collaboration with international organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian02-15_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian02-15-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, in May 2016 it was announced that Jolie-Pitt and Hague would join Jane Connors and Madeleine Rees as Visiting Professors in Practice from September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LSE has academic partnerships in teaching and research with six universities – with <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> in New York City and <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a>, in Asia with <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a> in Beijing and the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a>, in Africa with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town" title="University of Cape Town">University of Cape Town</a> and Europe with <a href="/wiki/Sciences_Po_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="Sciences Po Paris">Sciences Po</a> in Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Together they offer a range of double or joint degree programmes including an MA in International and World History (with Columbia) and an MSc in International Affairs with <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>, with graduates earning degrees from both institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The School also offers joint degrees for specific departments with various other universities including <a href="/wiki/Fudan_University" title="Fudan University">Fudan University</a> in Shanghai, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a> in Los Angeles and a Global Studies programme which is offered with a consortium of four European universities – <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leipzig" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Vienna" title="University of Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Roskilde" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Roskilde">Roskilde</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wroclaw" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Wroclaw">Wroclaw</a>.  It offers the TRIUM Global Executive MBA programme<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> jointly with <a href="/wiki/Stern_School_of_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="Stern School of Business">Stern School of Business</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> and <a href="/wiki/HEC_School_of_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="HEC School of Management">HEC School of Management</a>, Paris. It is divided into six modules held in five international business locations over a 16-month period. LSE also offers a Dual <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Public_Administration" title="Master of Public Administration">Master of Public Administration</a> (MPA) with Global Public Policy Network schools such as Sciences Po Paris,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Hertie_School_of_Governance" class="mw-redirect" title="Hertie School of Governance">Hertie School of Governance</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a>.
</p><p>The school also runs exchange programmes with a number of international business schools through the Global Master's in Management programme and an undergraduate student exchange programme with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a> in Political Science. LSE is the only UK member school in the CEMS Alliance, and the LSE Global Master's in Management is the only programme in the UK to offer the CEMS Master's in International Management (CEMS MIM) as a double degree option, allowing students to study at one of 30 CEMS partner universities.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> It also participates in Key Action 1 of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>-wide <a href="/wiki/Erasmus%2B" title="Erasmus+">Erasmus+</a> programme, encouraging staff and student mobility for teaching, although not the other Key Actions in the programme.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The School is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Commonwealth_Universities" title="Association of Commonwealth Universities">Association of Commonwealth Universities</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Association_of_Professional_Schools_of_International_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="The Association of Professional Schools of International Affairs">Association of Professional Schools of International Affairs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/European_University_Association" title="European University Association">European University Association</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/G5_(universities)" title="G5 (universities)">G5</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Global_Alliance_in_Management_Education" title="Global Alliance in Management Education">Global Alliance in Management Education</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universities_UK" title="Universities UK">Universities UK</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and is sometimes considered part of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_triangle_(universities)" title="Golden triangle (universities)">'Golden Triangle'</a> of universities in south-east England, along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, and <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King's College London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Golden_Opportunities_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Golden_Opportunities-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Funding_Riches_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Funding_Riches-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Savage2015_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Savage2015-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian03_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian03-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OECD08_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD08-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THE02_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE02-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC2014_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2014-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_archives">Libraries and archives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Libraries and archives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22London+School+of+Economics%22">"London School of Economics"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22London+School+of+Economics%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22London+School+of+Economics%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22London+School+of+Economics%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22London+School+of+Economics%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22London+School+of+Economics%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lse_library_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/77/Lse_library_interior.jpg/220px-Lse_library_interior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/77/Lse_library_interior.jpg/330px-Lse_library_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/77/Lse_library_interior.jpg/440px-Lse_library_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lse_library_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of the main LSE library, designed by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Foster (architect)">Norman Foster</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_Library_of_Political_and_Economic_Science" title="British Library of Political and Economic Science">British Library of Political and Economic Science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Library" title="Women&#39;s Library">Women's Library</a></div>
<p>The School's main library, the <a href="/wiki/British_Library_of_Political_and_Economic_Science" title="British Library of Political and Economic Science">British Library of Political and Economic Science</a> is located in the <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Robbins" title="Lionel Robbins">Lionel Robbins</a> Building and contains over 4&#160;million print volumes, 60,000 online journals and 29,000 electronic books.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The Digital Library contains digitised material from LSE Library collections and also <a href="/wiki/Born-digital" title="Born-digital">born-digital</a> material that has been collected and preserved in digital formats.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Founded in 1896, it is the world's largest social and political sciences library and the national social science library of the United Kingdom and Commonwealth.  Its collections are recognised for their outstanding national and international status and hold 'Designation' status by the <a href="/wiki/Museums,_Libraries_and_Archives_Council" title="Museums, Libraries and Archives Council">Museums, Libraries and Archives Council</a> (MLA). BLPES responds to around 7,500 visits from students and staff each day. In addition, it provides a specialist international research collection, serving over 12,000 registered external users each year.
</p><p>The Shaw Library, housed in LSE's Founders Room in the Old Building contains the School's collection of fiction and general readings.  It also hosts a weekly series of lunchtime music concerts and press launches and is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Window" title="Fabian Window">Fabian Window</a> which was unveiled by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> in 2003.
</p><p>In 2013, LSE purchased the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Library" title="Women&#39;s Library">Women's Library</a>, Britain's main library and museum resource on women and the women's movement and a UNESCO classified resource from <a href="/wiki/London_Metropolitan_University" title="London Metropolitan University">London Metropolitan University</a>, moving the resources and artefacts into a new purpose-built facility within the Lionel Robbins Building complete with its own reading room and exhibition space. Several subject specific libraries also exist including the Seligman Library for Anthropology, the Himmelweit Library for Social Psychology, the Leverhulme Library for Statistics, the Robert McKenzie library for Sociology, the Michael Wise Library for Geography and the Gender Institute Library. Additionally, students are permitted to use the libraries of any other University of London college, and the extensive facilities at <a href="/wiki/Senate_House_(University_of_London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate House (University of London)">Senate House</a> Library, situated in <a href="/wiki/Russell_Square" title="Russell Square">Russell Square</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LSE_Summer_School">LSE Summer School</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: LSE Summer School">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The original LSE Summer School was established in 1989 and has since expanded to offer over 70 three-week courses in accounting, finance, economics, English language, international relations, government, law and management each July and August.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> It is advertised as the largest and one of the most well-established university Summer Schools of its kind in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In recent years, the School has expanded its summer schools both abroad and into executive education with the LSE-PKU Summer School in Beijing (run with <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>, the LSE-UCT July School in Cape Town (run with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town" title="University of Cape Town">University of Cape Town</a>) and the Executive Summer School at its London campus. In 2011, it also launched a Methods Summer Programme. Together these courses welcome over 5,000 participants from over 130 countries and some of the top colleges and universities around the world, as well as professionals from several multinational institutions. Participants are housed in LSE halls of residence or their overseas equivalents, and the Summer School provides a full social programme including guest lectures and receptions.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_lectures">Public lectures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Public lectures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Mandela,_2000_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Nelson_Mandela%2C_2000_%284%29.jpg/220px-Nelson_Mandela%2C_2000_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Nelson_Mandela%2C_2000_%284%29.jpg/330px-Nelson_Mandela%2C_2000_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Nelson_Mandela%2C_2000_%284%29.jpg/440px-Nelson_Mandela%2C_2000_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="389" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Mandela,_2000_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> arriving at LSE in 2000 to deliver a public lecture</div></div></div>
<p>Public lectures hosted by LSE Events office, are open to students, alumni and the general public. As well as leading academics and commentators, speakers frequently include prominent national and international figures such as ambassadors, CEOs, <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">Members of Parliament</a>, and heads of state. A number of these are broadcast live around the world via the School's website.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> LSE organises over 200 public events every year.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recent<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> prominent speakers have included <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Bernanke" title="Ben Bernanke">Ben Bernanke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">Noam Chomsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Craven" title="Philip Craven">Philip Craven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niall_Ferguson" title="Niall Ferguson">Niall Ferguson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Fox" title="Vicente Fox">Vicente Fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Gillard" title="Julia Gillard">Julia Gillard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Greenspan" title="Alan Greenspan">Alan Greenspan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenzin_Gyatso" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenzin Gyatso">Tenzin Gyatso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hsien_Loong" title="Lee Hsien Loong">Lee Hsien Loong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Harvey" title="David Harvey">David Harvey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Tirole" title="Jean Tirole">Jean Tirole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angelina_Jolie" title="Angelina Jolie">Angelina Jolie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Krugman" title="Paul Krugman">Paul Krugman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Medvedev" class="mw-redirect" title="Dmitri Medvedev">Dmitri Medvedev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Monti" title="Mario Monti">Mario Monti</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Osborne" title="George Osborne">George Osborne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peston" title="Robert Peston">Robert Peston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Pi%C3%B1era" title="Sebastián Piñera">Sebastián Piñera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Rudd" title="Kevin Rudd">Kevin Rudd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Sachs" title="Jeffrey Sachs">Jeffrey Sachs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schroeder" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerhard Schroeder">Gerhard Schroeder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mesa" title="Carlos Mesa">Carlos D. Mesa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Soros" title="George Soros">George Soros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rowan_Williams" title="Rowan Williams">Rowan Williams</a>.  Previously, the School has hosted figures including <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also a number of annual lecture series hosted by various departments. These include but are not limited to the <a href="/wiki/Malinowski_Memorial_Lecture" title="Malinowski Memorial Lecture">Malinowski Memorial Lectures</a> hosted by the Department of Anthropology, the <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Robbins" title="Lionel Robbins">Lionel Robbins</a> Memorial Lectures and the <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Miliband" title="Ralph Miliband">Ralph Miliband</a> programme.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iXXi_Briefings">iXXi Briefings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: iXXi Briefings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The iXXi Briefings (from 9/11, written in Roman numerals) are private discussions which are attended by around 40 distinguished people, chaired by <a href="/wiki/Meghnad_Desai,_Baron_Desai" title="Meghnad Desai, Baron Desai">Lord Desai</a>. At the briefings, two speakers talk for 15 minutes each before discussion is opened to all attendees, operating under <a href="/wiki/Chatham_House_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Chatham House Rules">Chatham House Rules</a>. iXXi briefings provide an opportunity for the LSE to exhibit its resources and engage with experts and prominent figures. The iXXi briefings are run by LSE Enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-London_School_of_Economics_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_School_of_Economics-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing">Publishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Publishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2018, the university launched LSE Press in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Ubiquity_Press" title="Ubiquity Press">Ubiquity Press</a>. This is intended to publish open-access journals and books in the social sciences. The first journal to be published by the press was the <i>Journal of Illicit Economies and Development</i>, edited by Dr John Collins, executive director of LSE's International Drug Policy Unit. The press is managed through the <a href="/wiki/British_Library_of_Political_and_Economic_Science" title="British Library of Political and Economic Science">LSE Library</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

assessment</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Teaching_Excellence_Framework" title="Teaching Excellence Framework">Teaching Excellence Framework</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-TEF_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TEF-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup></th><td><i>Bronze</i></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In overall <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">national rankings</a>, the LSE consistently placed as a top 15 university until 2019, when it fell to 19th in the Guardian table for 2020. It was placed joint 8th in the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> Table of Tables 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The LSE also ranked 3rd overall in the <i>Sunday Times University Guide</i> cumulative ranking over a ten-year period (1998–2007).<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline2007_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline2007-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> LSE was one of only eight universities (along with the other members of the <a href="/wiki/G5_(universities)" title="G5 (universities)">G5</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bath" title="University of Bath">Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warwick" title="University of Warwick">Warwick</a>) to have never left the top 15 in one of the three main domestic rankings between 2008–2017.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i> for 2016–17 rankings saw the LSE placed 37th overall. The 2016–17 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> ranked LSE 25th globally and placed it 5th in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> LSE was also ranked 24th for reputation by Times Higher Education in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> However, the 2016–17 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> placed the LSE 151–200 and 16–21 nationally, while the <a href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="US News &amp; World Report">US News &amp; World Report</a> <i>Best Global Universities 2017</i> placed it 261st globally and 30th in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The citation-based <a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking">CWTS Leiden Ranking</a> placed LSE 90th worldwide and 16th in the UK.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings"><i>Times Higher Education</i></a> 2017 ranks social sciences at LSE at 15th globally and 4th in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The <i>QS World University Rankings by Subject 2017</i> ranks the LSE second in the world for Social Sciences and Management and third in the world for Geography, Communication and Media Studies, Politics, and Social Policy and Administration. It is ranked in the top ten for Anthropology, Development studies, Accounting and Finance, History, Philosophy, Law, Economics, and Business and Management Studies, in the top 30 for Psychology, and the top 40 for Statistics.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Disparities between national and international league tables have caused LSE to offer public explanations for the difference, including the statement in 2012: 
</p>
<dl><dd><i>"At mid-2012, LSE has seen pleasing improvements over the last couple of years in our standing in all the main global rankings: those produced by Times Higher Education, QS and Shanghai Jiaotong University [the Academic Ranking of World Universities]. We have also seen good rises in the domestic UK rankings. But we remain concerned that all of the global rankings – by some way the most important for us, given our highly international orientation – suffer from inbuilt biases in favour of large multi-faculty universities with full STEM (Science, Technology, Engineering and Mathematics) offerings, and against small, specialist, mainly non-STEM universities such as LSE."<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup></i></dd></dl>
<p>According to data released by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Education" title="Department for Education">Department for Education</a> in 2018, LSE was rated as the best university for boosting graduate earnings, with male graduates seeing a 47.2% increase in earnings and female graduates seeing a 38.2% increase in earnings compared to the average graduate.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> According to Wealth-X and UBS's "Billionaire Census" in 2014, LSE ranked 10th in the list of 20 schools that have produced the most billionaire alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The LSE was the only UK university to make the list.
</p><p>In the 2017 <a href="/wiki/National_Student_Survey" title="National Student Survey">National Student Survey</a> LSE came 145th out of 148 for overall student satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg/220px-Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg/330px-Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg/440px-Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields_-_May_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>LSE students revising in <a href="/wiki/Lincoln%27s_Inn_Fields" title="Lincoln&#39;s Inn Fields">Lincoln's Inn Fields</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2015–16 academic year there were 10,833 full-time students and around 700 part-time students at the university. Of these, approximately 7,500 came from outside the United Kingdom (approximately 70% of the total student body), making LSE a highly international school with over 160 countries represented.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> LSE had more countries represented by students than the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> 32% of LSE's students come from Asia, 10% from North America, 2% each from South America and Africa. Combined over 100 languages are spoken at LSE.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Over half of LSE's students are postgraduates,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and there is approximately an equal split between genders with 51% male and 49% female students.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Alumni total over 160,000, covering over 190 countries with more than 80 active alumni groups.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Students.27_Union"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Students'_Union">Students' Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Students&#039; Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/LSE_Students%27_Union" title="LSE Students&#39; Union">LSE Students' Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg/220px-LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg/330px-LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg/440px-LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="266" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LSE_Students%27_Union_Logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The logo of LSE Students' Union</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/LSE_Students%27_Union" title="LSE Students&#39; Union">LSE Students' Union</a> (LSESU) is affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Students_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Union of Students (United Kingdom)">National Union of Students</a> and is responsible for campaigning and lobbying the School on behalf of students as well providing student support and the organisation and undertaking of entertainment events and student societies. It is often regarded as the most politically active in Britain – a reputation it has held since the well documented LSE student riots in 1966–67 and 1968–69,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> which made international headlines. In 2015, the School was awarded the top spot for student nightlife by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> newspaper<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> due in part to its central location and provision of over 200 societies, 40 sports clubs, a Raising and Giving (RAG) branch and a thriving media group. In 2013, the Union moved into a purpose-built new building – the Saw Swee Hock Student Centre on the Aldwych campus.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A weekly student newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beaver_(newspaper)" title="The Beaver (newspaper)">The Beaver</a></i>, is published each Tuesday during term time and is amongst the oldest student newspapers in the country. It sits alongside a radio station, <i><a href="/wiki/PuLSEfm" class="mw-redirect" title="PuLSEfm">Pulse!</a></i> which has existed since 1999 and a television station <i>LooSE Television</i> since 2005. The <i><a href="/wiki/Clare_Market_Review" title="Clare Market Review">Clare Market Review</a></i> one of Britain's oldest student publications was revived in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-LSESU_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSESU-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>  Over £150,000 is raised for charity each year through the RAG (Raising and Giving), the fundraising arm of the Students' Union,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> which was started in 1980 by then Student Union Entertainments Officer and former New Zealand MP <a href="/wiki/Tim_Barnett_(politician)" title="Tim Barnett (politician)">Tim Barnett</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sporting activity is coordinated by the LSE Athletics Union, which is a constituent of <a href="/wiki/British_Universities_%26_Colleges_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="British Universities &amp; Colleges Sport">British Universities &amp; Colleges Sport</a> (BUCS).<sup id="cite_ref-LSESU_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSESU-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NorthumberlandHouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/NorthumberlandHouse.jpg/170px-NorthumberlandHouse.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/NorthumberlandHouse.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NorthumberlandHouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northumberland House</div></div></div>
<p>LSE owns or operates 10 halls of residence in and around central London and there are also two halls owned by urbanest and five intercollegiate halls (shared with other constituent colleges of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>) within a 3-mile radius of the School, for a total of over 4,000 places.<sup id="cite_ref-Accommodation_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Accommodation-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Most residences take both undergraduates and postgraduates, although Carr-Saunders Hall and Passfield Hall are undergraduate only, and Butler's Wharf Residence, Grosvenor House and Lillian Knowles House are reserved for postgraduates. Sidney Webb House, managed by <a href="/wiki/Unite_Students" title="Unite Students">Unite Students</a>, takes postgraduates and continuing students.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> There are also flats available on Anson and Carleton roads, which are reserved for students with children.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The School guarantees accommodation for all first-year undergraduate students and many of the school's larger postgraduate population are also catered for, with some specific residences available for postgraduate living.<sup id="cite_ref-AccommodationAllocation_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccommodationAllocation-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Whilst none of the residences are located at the Aldwych campus, the closest, Grosvenor House is within a five-minute walk from the School in <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden" title="Covent Garden">Covent Garden</a>, whilst the farthest residences (Nutford and <a href="/wiki/Butler%27s_Wharf" title="Butler&#39;s Wharf">Butler's Wharf</a>) are approximately forty-five minutes by <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">Tube</a> or <a href="/wiki/London_Buses" title="London Buses">Bus</a>.
</p><p>Each residence accommodates a mixture of students both home and international, male and female, and, usually, undergraduate and postgraduate. New undergraduate students (including <a href="/wiki/The_General_Course" title="The General Course">General Course</a> students) occupy approximately 55% of all spaces, with postgraduates taking approximately 40% and continuing students about 5% of places.<sup id="cite_ref-AccommodationAllocation_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccommodationAllocation-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gh_new.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Gh_new.jpg/170px-Gh_new.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Gh_new.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="299" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gh_new.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grosvenor House Studios</div></div></div>
<p>The largest LSE student residence, Bankside House, a refurbished early 1950's office block and former headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Electricity_Generating_Board" title="Central Electricity Generating Board">Central Electricity Generating Board</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> opened to students in 1996 and is fully catered, accommodating 617 students across eight floors overlooking the River Thames. It is located behind the <a href="/wiki/Tate_Modern" title="Tate Modern">Tate Modern</a> art gallery on the south bank of the river.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The second-largest residence, the High Holborn Residence in <a href="/wiki/High_Holborn" title="High Holborn">High Holborn</a>, was opened in 1995 and is approximately 10 minutes walk from the main campus. It is self-catering, accommodating 447 students in flats of four our five bedrooms with shared facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Other accommodation is located in the surrounding area – Butler's Wharf is situated next to <a href="/wiki/Tower_Bridge" title="Tower Bridge">Tower Bridge</a>, Rosebery Hall is located in the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington" title="London Borough of Islington">London Borough of Islington</a> close to <a href="/wiki/Sadler%27s_Wells_Theatre" title="Sadler&#39;s Wells Theatre">Sadler's Wells</a>, and Carr-Saunders Hall, named after the LSE professor, is approximately 5&#160;minutes from <a href="/wiki/Telecom_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecom Tower">Telecom Tower</a> in the heart of <a href="/wiki/Fitzrovia" title="Fitzrovia">Fitzrovia</a>.
</p><p>Since 2005, the school has opened three new residences to provide accommodation for all first-year students. Lilian Knowles, independently operated in <a href="/wiki/Spitalfields" title="Spitalfields">Spitalfields</a>, is home for approximately 360 students and opened in 2006.  It is located in a converted Victorian night refuge; the remnants of which can still be seen on the outside facade.  It is a common stop on <a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Ripper" title="Jack the Ripper">Jack the Ripper</a> tours as one of his victims is commonly believed to have been a one-time resident. Planning permission was sought to convert the Grade II listed Northumberland House, on <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Avenue" title="Northumberland Avenue">Northumberland Avenue</a> into a new residence in June 2005, and the accommodation opened to students in October 2006. It was formerly a <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> grand hotel and lately government offices.
</p><p>The closest residence to the Aldwych campus is reserved for postgraduate students and is located on the eastern side of <a href="/wiki/Drury_Lane" title="Drury Lane">Drury Lane</a> at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Great_Queen_Street" title="Great Queen Street">Great Queen Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Acre_(street)" class="mw-redirect" title="Long Acre (street)">Long Acre</a>. Grosvenor House, converted from a Victorian office building, opened in September 2005. The residence is unique in that all of its 169 rooms are small, self-contained studios, with private toilet and shower facilities and a mini-kitchen.
</p>

<p>LSE has a long list of notable alumni and staff, spanning the fields of scholarship provided by the school.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The school has over 50 fellows of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy" title="British Academy">British Academy</a> on its staff, while other notable former staff members include <a href="/wiki/Brian_Barry" title="Brian Barry">Brian Barry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Cranston" title="Maurice Cranston">Maurice Cranston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Giddens" title="Anthony Giddens">Anthony Giddens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Laski" title="Harold Laski">Harold Laski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Miliband" title="Ralph Miliband">Ralph Miliband</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Oakeshott" title="Michael Oakeshott">Michael Oakeshott</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Phillips_(economist)" title="William Phillips (economist)">A. W. Philips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Popper" title="Karl Popper">Karl Popper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Robbins,_Baron_Robbins" class="mw-redirect" title="Lionel Robbins, Baron Robbins">Lionel Robbins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Strange" title="Susan Strange">Susan Strange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Ward_(communications_director)" title="Bob Ward (communications director)">Bob Ward</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Webster_(historian)" title="Charles Webster (historian)">Charles Webster</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mervyn_King,_Baron_King_of_Lothbury" title="Mervyn King, Baron King of Lothbury">Mervyn King</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Bank_of_England" title="Governor of the Bank of England">Governor of the Bank of England</a>, is also a former professor of economics.
</p><p>In the political arena notable alumni and staff include 53 past or present heads of state, 20 members of the current <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">British House of Commons</a> and 46 members of the current <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>. Former British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a> taught at the school from 1912 to 1923. In recent British politics, former LSE students include <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Bottomley" title="Virginia Bottomley">Virginia Bottomley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yvette_Cooper" title="Yvette Cooper">Yvette Cooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwina_Currie" title="Edwina Currie">Edwina Currie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Dobson" title="Frank Dobson">Frank Dobson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Hodge" title="Margaret Hodge">Margaret Hodge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kilroy-Silk" title="Robert Kilroy-Silk">Robert Kilroy-Silk</a> and former UK Labour Party leader <a href="/wiki/Ed_Miliband" title="Ed Miliband">Ed Miliband</a>. Internationally, Brazilian defence minister <a href="/wiki/Celso_Amorim" title="Celso Amorim">Celso Amorim</a>, Costa Rican President <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Arias" title="Óscar Arias">Óscar Arias</a>, Japanese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Taro_Aso" class="mw-redirect" title="Taro Aso">Taro Aso</a>, Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II of Denmark</a>, architect of the Indian Constitution and eminent economist <a href="/wiki/B._R._Ambedkar" title="B. R. Ambedkar">B. R. Ambedkar</a>, President of India <a href="/wiki/K._R._Narayanan" class="mw-redirect" title="K. R. Narayanan">K. R. Narayanan</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Taiwan" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Taiwan">President of Taiwan</a> <a href="/wiki/Tsai_Ing-wen" title="Tsai Ing-wen">Tsai Ing-wen</a>, Italian Prime Minister and President of the European Commission, <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>, French Foreign Minister and President of the Constitutional Council <a href="/wiki/Roland_Dumas" title="Roland Dumas">Roland Dumas</a><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> as well as Singapore's Deputy Prime Minister and Chairman of the International Monetary and Financial Committee at the International Monetary Fund (IMF), <a href="/wiki/Tharman_Shanmugaratnam" title="Tharman Shanmugaratnam">Tharman Shanmugaratnam</a> all studied at LSE. A notable number of LSE students have also played a role in the <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> administration, including <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rouse" title="Pete Rouse">Pete Rouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_R._Orszag" title="Peter R. Orszag">Peter R. Orszag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mona_Sutphen" title="Mona Sutphen">Mona Sutphen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Volcker" title="Paul Volcker">Paul Volcker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Furman" title="Jason Furman">Jason Furman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Physician <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Kerry" title="Vanessa Kerry">Vanessa Kerry</a> and American journalist <a href="/wiki/Susan_Rasky" title="Susan Rasky">Susan Rasky</a> are also alumnae of the LSE. Notable American <a href="/wiki/Monica_Lewinsky" title="Monica Lewinsky">Monica Lewinsky</a> pursued her MSc in Social Psychology at the LSE.
</p><p>Business people who studied at LSE include the CEO of <a href="/wiki/AirAsia" title="AirAsia">AirAsia</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fernandes" title="Tony Fernandes">Tony Fernandes</a>,  former CEO of <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Akerson" title="Daniel Akerson">Daniel Akerson</a>, Director of <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a> <a href="/wiki/Delphine_Arnault" title="Delphine Arnault">Delphine Arnault</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> <a href="/wiki/Stelios_Haji-Ioannou" title="Stelios Haji-Ioannou">Stelios Haji-Ioannou</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Abercrombie_%26_Fitch" title="Abercrombie &amp; Fitch">Abercrombie &amp; Fitch</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_S._Jeffries" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael S. Jeffries">Michael S. Jeffries</a>, Greek business magnate <a href="/wiki/Spiros_Latsis" title="Spiros Latsis">Spiros Latsis</a>, American banker <a href="/wiki/David_Rockefeller" title="David Rockefeller">David Rockefeller</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Newsmax_Media" title="Newsmax Media">Newsmax Media</a> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Ruddy" title="Christopher Ruddy">Christopher Ruddy</a>, founder of advertising agency <a href="/wiki/Saatchi_and_Saatchi" class="mw-redirect" title="Saatchi and Saatchi">Saatchi and Saatchi</a> <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Saatchi,_Baron_Saatchi" title="Maurice Saatchi, Baron Saatchi">Maurice Saatchi</a>, hedge fund managers <a href="/wiki/George_Soros" title="George Soros">George Soros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Platt_(finance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Platt (finance)">Michael Platt</a>.
</p><p>Convicted British terrorist, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Saeed_Sheikh" class="mw-redirect" title="Omar Saeed Sheikh">Omar Saeed Sheikh</a>, studied Statistics at LSE, but did not graduate. He served five years in an Indian prison for kidnapping British tourists in 1994. In 2002, he was arrested and convicted in the kidnapping and murder of <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Pearl" title="Daniel Pearl">Daniel Pearl</a>. <i>The Guardian</i> reported that Sheikh came into contact with radical Islamists at the LSE.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_15_July_2002_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_15_July_2002-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_laureates">Nobel laureates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_School_of_Economics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Nobel laureates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_the_London_School_of_Economics" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the London School of Economics">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the London School of Economics</a></div>
<p>As of 2019, 18 Nobel Prizes in economics, peace and literature are officially recognised as having been awarded to LSE alumni and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:18px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg/120px-Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="114" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg/180px-Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg/240px-Leonid_Hurwicz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1759" data-file-height="1672" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Leonid_Hurwicz" title="Leonid Hurwicz">Leonid Hurwicz</a> – <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel laureate">Nobel laureate</a> in Economics – studied at LSE with <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Kaldor" title="Nicholas Kaldor">Nicholas Kaldor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Hayek</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Pissarides.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Christopher_Pissarides.jpg/84px-Christopher_Pissarides.jpg" decoding="async" width="84" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Christopher_Pissarides.jpg/126px-Christopher_Pissarides.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Christopher_Pissarides.jpg/168px-Christopher_Pissarides.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3640" data-file-height="5200" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_A._Pissarides" title="Christopher A. Pissarides">Christopher A. Pissarides</a> – awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in Economics">Nobel Prize in Economics</a> in 2010 – currently <a href="/wiki/Regius_Professor" title="Regius Professor">Regius Professor</a> of Economics at LSE
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg/75px-Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg" decoding="async" width="75" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg/112px-Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg/150px-Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="320" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, Indian economist, former professor and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel laureate</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg/95px-Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="95" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg/142px-Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg/190px-Juan_Manuel_Santos_in_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="413" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a>, former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">president of Colombia</a> and recipient of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2016 Nobel Peace Prize">2016 Nobel Peace Prize</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
